<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Folk music</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>

<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>

<p><b>Folk music</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">music genre</a> that includes <a href="#Traditional_folk_music">traditional folk music</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_folk_music" title="Contemporary folk music">contemporary genre</a> that evolved from the former during the 20th-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Folk_revival" title="Folk revival">folk revival</a>. Some types of folk music may be called <a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">world music</a>. Traditional folk music has been defined in several ways: as music transmitted orally, music with unknown composers, music that is played on traditional instruments, music about cultural or national identity, music that changes between generations (folk process), music associated with a people's <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a>, or music performed by <a href="/wiki/Convention_(norm)" title="Convention (norm)">custom</a> over a long period of time. It has been contrasted with <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">commercial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art_music" title="Art music">classical styles</a>. The term originated in the 19th century, but folk music extends beyond that.
</p><p>Starting in the mid-20th century, a new form of popular folk music evolved<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> from traditional folk music. This process and period is called the (second) folk revival and reached a zenith in the 1960s. This form of music is sometimes called <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_folk_music" title="Contemporary folk music">contemporary folk music</a> or folk revival music to distinguish it from earlier folk forms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AboutDefinition_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-AboutDefinition-1">[1]</a></sup> Smaller, similar revivals have occurred elsewhere in the world at other times, but the term folk music has typically not been applied to the new music created during those revivals. This type of folk music also includes fusion genres such as <a href="/wiki/Folk_rock" title="Folk rock">folk rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Folk_metal" title="Folk metal">folk metal</a>, and others. While contemporary folk music is a genre generally distinct from traditional folk music, in <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">U.S. English</a> it shares the same name, and it often shares the same performers and venues as traditional folk music.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Folk_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The terms <i>folk music</i>, <i>folk song</i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Folk_dance" title="Folk dance">folk dance</a></i> are comparatively recent expressions. They are extensions of the term <i><a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a></i>, which was coined in 1846 by the English antiquarian <a href="/wiki/William_Thoms" title="William Thoms">William Thoms</a> to describe "the traditions, customs, and superstitions of the uncultured classes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Percy_Scholes_1977_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Percy_Scholes_1977-2">[2]</a></sup> The term further derives from the German expression <i><a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lkisch_movement" title="Völkisch movement">volk</a></i>, in the sense of "the people as a whole" as applied to popular and national music by <a href="/wiki/Johann_Gottfried_Herder" title="Johann Gottfried Herder">Johann Gottfried Herder</a> and the German Romantics over half a century earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Though it is understood that folk music is the music of the people, observers find a more precise definition to be elusive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NERevival_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-NERevival-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Some do not even agree that the term folk music should be used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NERevival_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-NERevival-4">[4]</a></sup> Folk music may tend to have certain characteristics<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Percy_Scholes_1977_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Percy_Scholes_1977-2">[2]</a></sup> but it cannot clearly be differentiated in purely musical terms. One meaning often given is that of "old songs, with no known composers,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ronald_D._Cohen_2006_pp._1-2_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ronald_D._Cohen_2006_pp._1-2-6">[6]</a></sup> another is that of music that has been submitted to an evolutionary "process of <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">oral transmission</a>.... the fashioning and re-fashioning of the music by the community that give it its folk character."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloyd_1969_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lloyd_1969-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>Such definitions depend upon "(cultural) processes rather than abstract musical types...", upon "<i>continuity</i> and <i>oral transmission</i>...seen as characterizing one side of a cultural dichotomy, the other side of which is found not only in the lower layers of feudal, capitalist and some oriental societies but also in 'primitive' societies and in parts of 'popular cultures'".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> One widely used definition is simply "Folk music is what the people sing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Donaldson,_2011_page_13_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Donaldson,_2011_page_13-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>For Scholes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Percy_Scholes_1977_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Percy_Scholes_1977-2">[2]</a></sup> as well as for <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Sharp" title="Cecil Sharp">Cecil Sharp</a> and <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Bart%C3%B3k" title="Béla Bartók">Béla Bartók</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A.L.Lloyd,_1969,_pp._14-5_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-A.L.Lloyd,_1969,_pp._14-5-10">[10]</a></sup> there was a sense of the music of the country as distinct from that of the town. Folk music was already, "...seen as the authentic expression of a way of life now past or about to disappear (or in some cases, to be preserved or somehow revived),"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> particularly in "a community uninfluenced by art music"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lloyd_1969_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lloyd_1969-7">[7]</a></sup> and by commercial and printed song. Lloyd rejected this in favor of a simple distinction of economic class<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A.L.Lloyd,_1969,_pp._14-5_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-A.L.Lloyd,_1969,_pp._14-5-10">[10]</a></sup> yet for him, true folk music was, in <a href="/wiki/Charles_Seeger" title="Charles Seeger">Charles Seeger</a>'s words, "associated with a lower class"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-12">[12]</a></sup> in culturally and socially stratified societies. In these terms, folk music may be seen as part of a "schema comprising four musical types: 'primitive' or 'tribal'; 'elite' or 'art'; 'folk'; and 'popular'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charles_Seeger_1980_p.127_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Charles_Seeger_1980_p.127-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>Music in this genre is also often called <i>traditional music.</i> Although the term is usually only descriptive, in some cases people use it as the name of a genre. For example, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> previously used the terms "traditional music" and "traditional folk" for folk music that is not contemporary folk music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Folk music may include most <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_music" title="Indigenous music">indigenous music</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NERevival_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-NERevival-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">Characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Folk_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Viljandi_2010_002.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Viljandi_2010_002.jpg/220px-Viljandi_2010_002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Viljandi_2010_002.jpg/330px-Viljandi_2010_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Viljandi_2010_002.jpg/440px-Viljandi_2010_002.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Viljandi_2010_002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Viljandi_Folk_Music_Festival" title="Viljandi Folk Music Festival">Viljandi Folk Music Festival</a> held annually within the castle ruins in <a href="/wiki/Viljandi" title="Viljandi">Viljandi</a>, Estonia.</div></div></div>
<p>From a historical perspective, traditional folk music had these characteristics:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mills_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mills-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>It was transmitted through an <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">oral tradition</a>. Before the 20th century, ordinary people were usually illiterate; they acquired songs by memorizing them. Primarily, this was not mediated by books or recorded or transmitted media. Singers may extend their repertoire using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadside_(music)" title="Broadside (music)">broadsheets</a> or <a href="/wiki/Song_book" title="Song book">song books</a>, but these secondary enhancements are of the same character as the primary songs experienced in the flesh.</li>
<li>The music was often related to <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">national culture</a>. It was culturally particular; from a particular region or culture. In the context of an immigrant group, folk music acquires an extra dimension for social cohesion. It is particularly conspicuous in immigrant societies, where <a href="/wiki/Greek_Australians" title="Greek Australians">Greek Australians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somali_Americans" title="Somali Americans">Somali Americans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_Canadians" title="Punjabi Canadians">Punjabi Canadians</a>, and others strive to emphasize their differences from the mainstream. They learn songs and dances that originate in the countries their grandparents came from.</li>
<li>They commemorate historical and personal events. On certain days of the year, including such holidays as Christmas, Easter, and May Day, particular songs celebrate the yearly cycle. Birthdays, weddings, and funerals may also be noted with songs, dances and special costumes. Religious festivals often have a folk music component. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Choral_music" title="Choral music">Choral music</a> at these events brings children and non-professional singers to participate in a public arena, giving an emotional bonding that is unrelated to the aesthetic qualities of the music.</li>
<li>The songs have been performed, by <a href="/wiki/Convention_(norm)" title="Convention (norm)">custom</a>, over a long period of time, usually several <a href="/wiki/Generation" title="Generation">generations</a>.</li></ul>
<p>As a side-effect, the following characteristics are sometimes present:
</p>
<ul><li>There is no <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">copyright</a> on the songs. Hundreds of folk songs from the 19th century have known authors but have continued in oral tradition to the point where they are considered traditional for purposes of music publishing. This has become much less frequent since the 1940s. Today, almost every folk song that is recorded is credited with an arranger.</li>
<li>Fusion of cultures: Because cultures interact and change over time, traditional songs evolving over time may incorporate and reflect influences from disparate cultures. The relevant factors may include instrumentation, <a href="/wiki/Musical_tuning" title="Musical tuning">tunings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Voicing_(music)" title="Voicing (music)">voicings</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phrasing_(music)" title="Phrasing (music)">phrasing</a>, subject matter, and even production methods.</li></ul>
<p><br/>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tune">Tune</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Folk_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tune">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In folk music, a <i>tune</i> is a short <a href="/wiki/Instrumental" title="Instrumental">instrumental</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piece_(music)" title="Piece (music)">piece</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Melody" title="Melody">melody</a>, often with repeating <a href="/wiki/Section_(music)" title="Section (music)">sections</a>, and usually played a number of times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> A collection of tunes with structural similarities is known as a <a href="/wiki/Tune-family" title="Tune-family">tune-family</a>. <i>America's Musical Landscape</i> says "the most common <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Form_(music)" title="Form (music)">form</a> for tunes in folk music is AABB, also known as <a href="/wiki/Binary_form" title="Binary form">binary form</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>In some traditions, tunes may be strung together in <a href="/wiki/Medley_(music)" title="Medley (music)">medleys</a> or "<a href="/wiki/Set_(music)" title="Set (music)">sets</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Folk_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Indian_village_musicians.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="610" data-file-width="810" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Indian_village_musicians.jpg/220px-Indian_village_musicians.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Indian_village_musicians.jpg/330px-Indian_village_musicians.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Indian_village_musicians.jpg/440px-Indian_village_musicians.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Indian_village_musicians.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Indians always distinguished between classical and folk music, though in the past even classical Indian music used to rely on the unwritten transmission of repertoire.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Navneet-Aditya-Waiba-Live.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2997" data-file-width="2997" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Navneet-Aditya-Waiba-Live.jpg/220px-Navneet-Aditya-Waiba-Live.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Navneet-Aditya-Waiba-Live.jpg/330px-Navneet-Aditya-Waiba-Live.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Navneet-Aditya-Waiba-Live.jpg/440px-Navneet-Aditya-Waiba-Live.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Navneet-Aditya-Waiba-Live.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Indian Nepali folk musician <a href="/wiki/Navneet_Aditya_Waiba" title="Navneet Aditya Waiba">Navneet Aditya Waiba</a></div></div></div>
<p>Throughout most of human prehistory and history, listening to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recorded_music" title="Recorded music">recorded music</a> was not possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Music was made by common people during both their work and leisure, as well as during religious activities. The work of economic production was often manual and communal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manual_labor" title="Manual labor">Manual labor</a> often included singing by the workers, which served several practical purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> It reduced the <a href="/wiki/Boredom" title="Boredom">boredom</a> of repetitive tasks, it kept the <a href="/wiki/Rhythm" title="Rhythm">rhythm</a> during <a href="/wiki/Synchronization" title="Synchronization">synchronized</a> pushes and pulls, and it set the pace of many activities such as <a href="/wiki/Sowing" title="Sowing">planting</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weeding" title="Weeding">weeding</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reaping" title="Reaping">reaping</a>, <a href="/wiki/Threshing" title="Threshing">threshing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weaving" title="Weaving">weaving</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milling_(grinding)" title="Milling (grinding)">milling</a>. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leisure_time" title="Leisure time">leisure time</a>, singing and playing <a href="/wiki/Musical_instrument" title="Musical instrument">musical instruments</a> were common forms of entertainment and history-telling—even more common than today when electrically enabled technologies and widespread literacy make other forms of entertainment and information-sharing competitive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SeegerLomaxDocumentary_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-SeegerLomaxDocumentary-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some believe that folk music originated as <a href="/wiki/Art_music" title="Art music">art music</a> that was changed and probably debased by oral transmission while reflecting the character of the society that produced it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Percy_Scholes_1977_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-Percy_Scholes_1977-2">[2]</a></sup> In many societies, especially preliterate ones, the cultural transmission of folk music requires <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Learning_music_by_ear" title="Learning music by ear">learning by ear</a>, although <a href="/wiki/Musical_notation" title="Musical notation">notation</a> has evolved in some cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Different cultures may have different notions concerning a division between "folk" music on the one hand and of "art" and "court" music on the other. In the proliferation of popular music genres, some traditional folk music became also referred to as "<a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">World music</a>" or "Roots music".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>The English term "<a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a>", to describe traditional folk music and dance, entered the vocabulary of many continental European nations, each of which had its folk-song collectors and revivalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Percy_Scholes_1977_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-Percy_Scholes_1977-2">[2]</a></sup> The distinction between "authentic" folk and national and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Popular_song" title="Popular song">popular song</a> in general has always been loose, particularly in America and Germany<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Percy_Scholes_1977_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-Percy_Scholes_1977-2">[2]</a></sup> – for example, popular songwriters such as <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Foster" title="Stephen Foster">Stephen Foster</a> could be termed "folk" in America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Percy_Scholes_1977_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-Percy_Scholes_1977-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Folk_Music_Council" title="International Folk Music Council">International Folk Music Council</a> definition allows that the term can also apply to music that, "...has originated with an individual composer and has subsequently been absorbed into the unwritten, living tradition of a community. But the term does not cover a song, dance, or tune that has been taken over ready-made and remains unchanged."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>The post–<a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> folk revival in America and in Britain started a new genre, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contemporary_Folk_Music" title="Contemporary Folk Music">Contemporary Folk Music</a>, and brought an additional meaning to the term "folk music": newly composed songs, fixed in form and by known authors, which imitated some form of traditional music. The popularity of "contemporary folk" recordings caused the appearance of the category "Folk" in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a> of 1959;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> in 1970 the term was dropped in favor of "Best Ethnic or Traditional Recording (including Traditional Blues)",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> while 1987 brought a distinction between "Best Traditional Folk Recording" and "Best Contemporary Folk Recording".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> After that, they had a "Traditional music" category that subsequently evolved into others. The term "folk", by the start of the 21st century, could cover singer-songwriters, such as <a href="/wiki/Donovan" title="Donovan">Donovan</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> from Scotland and American <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> who emerged in the 1960s and much more. This completed a process to where "folk music" no longer meant only traditional folk music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ronald_D._Cohen_2006_pp._1-2_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ronald_D._Cohen_2006_pp._1-2-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subject_matter">Subject matter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Folk_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Subject matter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Armenian_Musicians.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="308" data-file-width="402" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Armenian_Musicians.jpg/220px-Armenian_Musicians.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Armenian_Musicians.jpg/330px-Armenian_Musicians.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/63/Armenian_Musicians.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Armenian_Musicians.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian_culture" title="Armenian culture">Armenian</a> traditional musicians</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Assyrianfolk.jpg"><img alt="Assyrian folk music" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="164" data-file-width="230" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Assyrianfolk.jpg/220px-Assyrianfolk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6a/Assyrianfolk.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Assyrianfolk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a> playing <i><a href="/wiki/Zurna" title="Zurna">zurna</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Davul" title="Davul">Davul</a></i>, the typically used instruments for their folk music and <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_folk_dance" title="Assyrian folk dance">dance</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Traditional folk music often includes <a href="/wiki/Lyrics" title="Lyrics">sung words</a>, although folk <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Instrumental_music" title="Instrumental music">instrumental music</a> occurs commonly in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dancing_music" title="Dancing music">dance music</a> traditions. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narrative_verse" title="Narrative verse">Narrative verse</a> looms large in the traditional folk music of many cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> This encompasses such forms as traditional <a href="/wiki/Epic_poetry" title="Epic poetry">epic poetry</a>, much of which was meant originally for oral performance, sometimes accompanied by instruments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Many epic poems of various cultures were pieced together from shorter pieces of traditional narrative verse, which explains their episodic structure, repetitive elements, and their frequent <i><a href="/wiki/In_medias_res" title="In medias res">in medias res</a></i> plot developments. Other forms of traditional narrative verse relate the outcomes of <a href="/wiki/Battle" title="Battle">battles</a> or lament <a href="/wiki/Tragedy_(event)" title="Tragedy (event)">tragedies</a> or <a href="/wiki/Natural_disaster" title="Natural disaster">natural disasters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sometimes, as in the triumphant <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Song_of_Deborah" title="Song of Deborah">Song of Deborah</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> found in the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Biblical</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Judges" title="Book of Judges">Book of Judges</a></i>, these songs celebrate victory. Laments for lost battles and wars, and the lives lost in them, are equally prominent in many traditions; these laments keep alive the cause for which the battle was fought.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The narratives of traditional songs often also remember <a href="/wiki/Folk_hero" title="Folk hero">folk heroes</a> such as <a href="/wiki/John_Henry_(folklore)" title="John Henry (folklore)">John Henry</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood" title="Robin Hood">Robin Hood</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Some traditional song narratives recall <a href="/wiki/Supernatural" title="Supernatural">supernatural</a> events or mysterious deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hymn" title="Hymn">Hymns</a> and other forms of <a href="/wiki/Religious_music" title="Religious music">religious music</a> are often of traditional and unknown origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Western <a href="/wiki/Musical_notation" title="Musical notation">musical notation</a> was originally created to preserve the lines of <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_chant" title="Gregorian chant">Gregorian chant</a>, which before its invention was taught as an oral tradition in <a href="/wiki/Monasticism" title="Monasticism">monastic</a> communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Traditional songs such as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_grow_the_rushes,_O" title="Green grow the rushes, O">Green grow the rushes, O</a></i> present religious lore in a <a href="/wiki/Mnemonic" title="Mnemonic">mnemonic</a> form, as do Western <a href="/wiki/Christmas_carol" title="Christmas carol">Christmas carols</a> and similar traditional songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Work_song" title="Work song">Work songs</a> frequently feature <a href="/wiki/Call_and_response_(music)" title="Call and response (music)">call and response</a> structures and are designed to enable the laborers who sing them to coordinate their efforts in accordance with the rhythms of the songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> They are frequently, but not invariably, composed. In the American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armed_force" title="Armed force">armed forces</a>, a lively oral tradition preserves <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jody_call" title="Jody call">jody calls</a> ("Duckworth chants") which are sung while soldiers are on the march.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Professional sailors made similar use of a large body of <a href="/wiki/Sea_shanty" title="Sea shanty">sea shanties</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Love_poetry" title="Love poetry">Love poetry</a>, often of a tragic or regretful nature, prominently figures in many folk traditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nursery_rhyme" title="Nursery rhyme">Nursery rhymes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nonsense_verse" title="Nonsense verse">nonsense verse</a> used to amuse or quiet children also are frequent subjects of traditional songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Folk_song_transformations_and_variations">Folk song transformations and variations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Folk_music&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Folk song transformations and variations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_folk_music_traditions" title="List of folk music traditions">List of folk music traditions</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output
